package casbin

import (
	"testing"
)

func testEnforceLBAC(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, res bool) {
	t.Helper()
	if myRes, err := e.Enforce(sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act); err != nil {
		t.Errorf("Enforce Error: %s", err)
	} else if myRes != res {
		t.Errorf("%s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s: %t, supposed to be %t", sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act, myRes, res)
	}
}

func TestLBACModel(t *testing.T) {
	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/lbac_model.conf")

	t.Log("Testing normal read operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_topsecret", 3, 3, "read", true) // both high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", true)  // confidentiality equal, integrity higher
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 2, 3, "read", true)  // confidentiality higher, integrity equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "read", true)    // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing read operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", false)      // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_sensitive", 3, 5, "read", false) // insufficient integrity level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_internal", 3, 1, "read", false)    // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_protected", 1, 4, "read", false)   // insufficient integrity level

	t.Log("Testing normal write operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", true)   // both dimensions equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 5, 4, "write", true) // both low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 5, "write", true) // confidentiality equal, integrity low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_archive", 5, 5, "write", true)  // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing write operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_internal", 3, 5, "write", false) // confidentiality level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", false)     // both dimensions too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_secret", 5, 4, "write", false)     // integrity level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_private", 1, 3, "write", false)    // confidentiality level too high
}

2025-12-26 19:51:38,708 - INFO - swea-agent-casbin__casbin-1522 - 💭 THOUGHT
Good! So we have BLP and BIBA test files but no LBAC test file. Now let's understand LBAC better:

LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) is a security model that combines multiple security dimensions. According to Wikipedia and the model, LBAC combines:
1. **Confidentiality levels** (like in BLP - Bell-LaPadula model)
2. **Integrity levels** (like in BIBA model)

The rules are:
- For **read** operations: subject must have BOTH higher/equal confidentiality AND higher/equal integrity than the object
- For **write** operations: subject must have BOTH lower/equal confidentiality AND lower/equal integrity than the object

Now let me run the existing tests to make sure everything works before adding LBAC:

package casbin

import (
	"testing"
)

func testEnforceLBAC(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, res bool) {
	t.Helper()
	if myRes, err := e.Enforce(sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act); err != nil {
		t.Errorf("Enforce Error: %s", err)
	} else if myRes != res {
		t.Errorf("%s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s: %t, supposed to be %t", sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act, myRes, res)
	}
}

func TestLBACModel(t *testing.T) {
	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/lbac_model.conf")

	t.Log("Testing normal read operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_topsecret", 3, 3, "read", true) // both high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", true)  // confidentiality equal, integrity higher
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 2, 3, "read", true)  // confidentiality higher, integrity equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "read", true)    // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing read operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", false)      // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_sensitive", 3, 5, "read", false) // insufficient integrity level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_internal", 3, 1, "read", false)    // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_protected", 1, 4, "read", false)   // insufficient integrity level

	t.Log("Testing normal write operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", true)   // both dimensions equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 5, 4, "write", true) // both low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 5, "write", true) // confidentiality equal, integrity low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_archive", 5, 5, "write", true)  // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing write operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_internal", 3, 5, "write", false) // confidentiality level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", false)     // both dimensions too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_secret", 5, 4, "write", false)     // integrity level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_private", 1, 3, "write", false)    // confidentiality level too high
}
'

package casbin

import (
	"testing"
)

func testEnforceLBAC(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, res bool) {
	t.Helper()
	if myRes, err := e.Enforce(sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act); err != nil {
		t.Errorf("Enforce Error: %s", err)
	} else if myRes != res {
		t.Errorf("%s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s: %t, supposed to be %t", sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act, myRes, res)
	}
}

func TestLBACModel(t *testing.T) {
	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/lbac_model.conf")

	t.Log("Testing normal read operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_topsecret", 3, 3, "read", true) // both high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", true)  // confidentiality equal, integrity higher
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 2, 3, "read", true)  // confidentiality higher, integrity equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "read", true)    // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing read operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", false)      // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_sensitive", 3, 5, "read", false) // insufficient integrity level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_internal", 3, 1, "read", false)    // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_protected", 1, 4, "read", false)   // insufficient integrity level

	t.Log("Testing normal write operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", true)   // both dimensions equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 5, 4, "write", true) // both low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 5, "write", true) // confidentiality equal, integrity low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_archive", 5, 5, "write", true)  // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing write operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_internal", 3, 5, "write", false) // confidentiality level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", false)     // both dimensions too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_secret", 5, 4, "write", false)     // integrity level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_private", 1, 3, "write", false)    // confidentiality level too high
}
'

package casbin

import (
	"testing"
)

func testEnforceLBAC(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, res bool) {
	t.Helper()
	if myRes, err := e.Enforce(sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act); err != nil {
		t.Errorf("Enforce Error: %s", err)
	} else if myRes != res {
		t.Errorf("%s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s: %t, supposed to be %t", sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act, myRes, res)
	}
}

func TestLBACModel(t *testing.T) {
	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/lbac_model.conf")

	t.Log("Testing normal read operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_topsecret", 3, 3, "read", true) // both high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", true)  // confidentiality equal, integrity higher
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 2, 3, "read", true)  // confidentiality higher, integrity equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "read", true)    // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing read operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", false)      // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_sensitive", 3, 5, "read", false) // insufficient integrity level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_internal", 3, 1, "read", false)    // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_protected", 1, 4, "read", false)   // insufficient integrity level

	t.Log("Testing normal write operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", true)   // both dimensions equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 5, 4, "write", true) // both low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 5, "write", true) // confidentiality equal, integrity low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_archive", 5, 5, "write", true)  // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing write operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_internal", 3, 5, "write", false) // confidentiality level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", false)     // both dimensions too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_secret", 5, 4, "write", false)     // integrity level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_private", 1, 3, "write", false)    // confidentiality level too high
}

Perfect! All three tests pass. Now let me write a script to demonstrate that the LBAC model works correctly and understand how it functions:

🎬 ACTION
cat > /tmp/test_lbac.go << 'EOF'
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"log"

	"github.com/casbin/casbin/v2"
)

func main() {
	// Initialize the enforcer with LBAC model
	e, err := casbin.NewEnforcer("/testbed/examples/lbac_model.conf")
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Failed to create enforcer: %v", err)
	}

	fmt.Println("LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) Model Test")
	fmt.Println("==============================================")
	fmt.Println()
	
	fmt.Println("LBAC combines confidentiality (like BLP) and integrity (like BIBA)")
	fmt.Println("Read: subject must have >= confidentiality AND >= integrity than object")
	fmt.Println("Write: subject must have <= confidentiality AND <= integrity than object")
	fmt.Println()

	// Test read operations
	fmt.Println("Test 1: Admin (conf=5, integ=5) reading file_topsecret (conf=3, integ=3)")
	result, err := e.Enforce("admin", float64(5), float64(5), "file_topsecret", float64(3), float64(3), "read")
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Enforce error: %v", err)
	}
	fmt.Printf("Result: %v (Expected: true - both dimensions are higher)\n\n", result)

	fmt.Println("Test 2: Staff (conf=3, integ=3) reading file_secret (conf=4, integ=2)")
	result, err = e.Enforce("staff", float64(3), float64(3), "file_secret", float64(4), float64(2), "read")
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Enforce error: %v", err)
	}
	fmt.Printf("Result: %v (Expected: false - confidentiality too low)\n\n", result)

	fmt.Println("Test 3: Manager (conf=4, integ=4) reading file_sensitive (conf=3, integ=5)")
	result, err = e.Enforce("manager", float64(4), float64(4), "file_sensitive", float64(3), float64(5), "read")
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Enforce error: %v", err)
	}
	fmt.Printf("Result: %v (Expected: false - integrity too low)\n\n", result)

	// Test write operations
	fmt.Println("Test 4: Guest (conf=2, integ=2) writing to file_public (conf=2, integ=2)")
	result, err = e.Enforce("guest", float64(2), float64(2), "file_public", float64(2), float64(2), "write")
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Enforce error: %v", err)
	}
	fmt.Printf("Result: %v (Expected: true - both dimensions equal)\n\n", result)

	fmt.Println("Test 5: Staff (conf=3, integ=3) writing to file_internal (conf=5, integ=4)")
	result, err = e.Enforce("staff", float64(3), float64(3), "file_internal", float64(5), float64(4), "write")
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Enforce error: %v", err)
	}
	fmt.Printf("Result: %v (Expected: true - both dimensions are lower)\n\n", result)

	fmt.Println("Test 6: Staff (conf=3, integ=3) writing to file_public (conf=2, integ=2)")
	result, err = e.Enforce("staff", float64(3), float64(3), "file_public", float64(2), float64(2), "write")
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Enforce error: %v", err)
	}
	fmt.Printf("Result: %v (Expected: false - both dimensions too high)\n\n", result)

	fmt.Println("All tests completed successfully!")
}
EOF

package casbin

import (
	"testing"
)

func testEnforceLBAC(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, res bool) {
	t.Helper()
	if myRes, err := e.Enforce(sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act); err != nil {
		t.Errorf("Enforce Error: %s", err)
	} else if myRes != res {
		t.Errorf("%s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s: %t, supposed to be %t", sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act, myRes, res)
	}
}

func TestLBACModel(t *testing.T) {
	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/lbac_model.conf")

	t.Log("Testing normal read operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_topsecret", 3, 3, "read", true) // both high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", true)  // confidentiality equal, integrity higher
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 2, 3, "read", true)  // confidentiality higher, integrity equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "read", true)    // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing read operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", false)      // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_sensitive", 3, 5, "read", false) // insufficient integrity level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_internal", 3, 1, "read", false)    // insufficient confidentiality level
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_protected", 1, 4, "read", false)   // insufficient integrity level

	t.Log("Testing normal write operation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", true)   // both dimensions equal
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 5, 4, "write", true) // both low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 5, "write", true) // confidentiality equal, integrity low
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_archive", 5, 5, "write", true)  // both dimensions equal

	t.Log("Testing write operation violation scenarios")
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_internal", 3, 5, "write", false) // confidentiality level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", false)     // both dimensions too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_secret", 5, 4, "write", false)     // integrity level too high
	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_private", 1, 3, "write", false)    // confidentiality level too high
}

# LBAC Implementation Analysis

## Overview
LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) combines two security dimensions:
1. **Confidentiality** (like BLP - Bell-LaPadula)
2. **Integrity** (like BIBA)

## Implementation Approach: Option-2

This implementation follows **Option-2**, which means:
- NO modification to Casbin core enforce code
- Uses existing Casbin functionality
- All logic is encoded in the model's matcher expression

## The Model Configuration

### Request Definition
```
r = sub, subject_confidentiality, subject_integrity, obj, object_confidentiality, object_integrity, act
```
The request includes:
- Subject name
- Subject's confidentiality level
- Subject's integrity level
- Object name
- Object's confidentiality level
- Object's integrity level
- Action

### Matcher Expression
```
m = (r.act == "read" && r.subject_confidentiality >= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity >= r.object_integrity) 
    || (r.act == "write" && r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)
```

This matcher implements LBAC rules entirely in the expression:
- **Read**: subject must have BOTH >= confidentiality AND >= integrity
- **Write**: subject must have BOTH <= confidentiality AND <= integrity

## Key Points

1. **No Core Changes**: The implementation doesn't require any modifications to the Casbin enforcer
2. **Declarative**: All security logic is defined declaratively in the model
3. **Composable**: Combines BLP (confidentiality) and BIBA (integrity) constraints
4. **Casbin Editor Compatible**: Since it uses standard Casbin features, it works 100% with the Casbin editor

## Comparison with BLP and BIBA

### BLP (Bell-LaPadula) - Confidentiality Only
```
m = (r.act == "read" && r.sub_level >= r.obj_level) || (r.act == "write" && r.sub_level <= r.obj_level)
```

### BIBA - Integrity Only
```
m = (r.act == "read" && r.sub_level <= r.obj_level) || (r.act == "write" && r.sub_level >= r.obj_level)
```

### LBAC - Both Dimensions
```
m = (r.act == "read" && r.subject_confidentiality >= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity >= r.object_integrity) 
    || (r.act == "write" && r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)
```

LBAC essentially requires BOTH BLP (for confidentiality) AND BIBA (for integrity) to be satisfied.

## Conclusion
This is a clean Option-2 implementation that leverages Casbin's existing expression evaluation capabilities without requiring any core changes.
EOF

1. **Confidentiality** (like BLP - Bell-LaPadula)
2. **Integrity** (like BIBA)

## Implementation Approach: Option-2

- NO modification to Casbin core enforce code
- Uses existing Casbin functionality

## The Model Configuration

```
r = sub, subject_confidentiality, subject_integrity, obj, object_confidentiality, object_integrity, act
```

- Subject name
- Subject's confidentiality level
- Subject's integrity level
- Object name
- Object's confidentiality level
- Object's integrity level
- Action

### Matcher Expression
```
m = (r.act == "read" && r.subject_confidentiality >= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity >= r.object_integrity) 
    || (r.act == "write" && r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)
```

This matcher implements LBAC rules entirely in the expression:
- **Read**: subject must have BOTH >= confidentiality AND >= integrity
- **Write**: subject must have BOTH <= confidentiality AND <= integrity

## Key Points

1. **No Core Changes**: The implementation doesn't require any modifications to the Casbin enforcer
2. **Declarative**: All security logic is defined declaratively in the model
3. **Composable**: Combines BLP (confidentiality) and BIBA (integrity) constraints
4. **Casbin Editor Compatible**: Since it uses standard Casbin features, it works 100% with the Casbin editor

## Comparison with BLP and BIBA

### BLP (Bell-LaPadula) - Confidentiality Only
```
m = (r.act == "read" && r.sub_level >= r.obj_level) || (r.act == "write" && r.sub_level <= r.obj_level)
```

### BIBA - Integrity Only
```

```

### LBAC - Both Dimensions

```
    || (r.act == "write" && r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)
```

LBAC essentially requires BOTH BLP (for confidentiality) AND BIBA (for integrity) to be satisfied.

## Conclusion

cat > /tmp/verify_lbac_coverage.go << 'EOF'
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"log"

	"github.com/casbin/casbin/v2"
)

func testCase(e *casbin.Enforcer, testNum int, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, expected bool, description string) {
	result, err := e.Enforce(sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act)
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Test %d error: %v", testNum, err)
	}
	
	status := "✓ PASS"
	if result != expected {
		status = "✗ FAIL"
	}
	
	fmt.Printf("Test %d: %s\n", testNum, status)
	fmt.Printf("  Subject: %s (conf=%v, integ=%v)\n", sub, subConf, subInteg)
	fmt.Printf("  Object: %s (conf=%v, integ=%v)\n", obj, objConf, objInteg)
	fmt.Printf("  Action: %s\n", act)
	fmt.Printf("  Expected: %v, Got: %v\n", expected, result)
	fmt.Printf("  Description: %s\n\n", description)
	
	if result != expected {
		log.Fatalf("Test %d failed!", testNum)
	}
}

func main() {
	e, err := casbin.NewEnforcer("/testbed/examples/lbac_model.conf")
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Failed to create enforcer: %v", err)
	}

	fmt.Println("LBAC Model Comprehensive Test Suite")
	fmt.Println("====================================\n")

	// Read operations - should succeed
	fmt.Println("=== READ OPERATIONS - SHOULD SUCCEED ===\n")
	
	testCase(e, 1, "admin", 5, 5, "file1", 3, 3, "read", true,
		"High confidentiality and high integrity can read lower levels")
	
	testCase(e, 2, "user", 4, 4, "file2", 4, 2, "read", true,
		"Equal confidentiality, higher integrity can read")
	
	testCase(e, 3, "user", 3, 3, "file3", 2, 3, "read", true,
		"Higher confidentiality, equal integrity can read")
	
	testCase(e, 4, "user", 2, 2, "file4", 2, 2, "read", true,
		"Equal levels on both dimensions can read")
	
	// Read operations - should fail
	fmt.Println("=== READ OPERATIONS - SHOULD FAIL ===\n")
	
	testCase(e, 5, "user", 3, 3, "file5", 4, 2, "read", false,
		"Insufficient confidentiality level")
	
	testCase(e, 6, "user", 4, 4, "file6", 3, 5, "read", false,
		"Insufficient integrity level")
	
	testCase(e, 7, "user", 2, 2, "file7", 3, 1, "read", false,
		"Insufficient confidentiality level (integrity is higher)")
	
	testCase(e, 8, "user", 3, 3, "file8", 1, 4, "read", false,
		"Insufficient integrity level (confidentiality is higher)")
	
	// Write operations - should succeed
	fmt.Println("=== WRITE OPERATIONS - SHOULD SUCCEED ===\n")
	
	testCase(e, 9, "user", 2, 2, "file9", 2, 2, "write", true,
		"Equal levels on both dimensions can write")
	
	testCase(e, 10, "user", 3, 3, "file10", 5, 4, "write", true,
		"Lower confidentiality and lower integrity can write")
	
	testCase(e, 11, "user", 4, 4, "file11", 4, 5, "write", true,
		"Equal confidentiality, lower integrity can write")
	
	testCase(e, 12, "admin", 5, 5, "file12", 5, 5, "write", true,
		"Equal levels on both dimensions can write")
	
	// Write operations - should fail
	fmt.Println("=== WRITE OPERATIONS - SHOULD FAIL ===\n")
	
	testCase(e, 13, "user", 4, 4, "file13", 3, 5, "write", false,
		"Confidentiality level too high for write")
	
	testCase(e, 14, "user", 3, 3, "file14", 2, 2, "write", false,
		"Both dimensions too high for write")
	
	testCase(e, 15, "admin", 5, 5, "file15", 5, 4, "write", false,
		"Integrity level too high for write")
	
	testCase(e, 16, "user", 2, 2, "file16", 1, 3, "write", false,
		"Confidentiality level too high (integrity is lower)")
	
	// Edge cases
	fmt.Println("=== EDGE CASES ===\n")
	
	testCase(e, 17, "user", 1, 1, "file17", 1, 1, "read", true,
		"Minimum levels - read")
	
	testCase(e, 18, "user", 1, 1, "file18", 1, 1, "write", true,
		"Minimum levels - write")
	
	testCase(e, 19, "admin", 10, 10, "file19", 10, 10, "read", true,
		"Maximum levels - read")
	
	testCase(e, 20, "admin", 10, 10, "file20", 10, 10, "write", true,
		"Maximum levels - write")
	
	fmt.Println("\n✓ All 20 test cases passed successfully!")
	fmt.Println("\nConclusion: LBAC model correctly implements lattice-based access control")
	fmt.Println("by combining confidentiality (BLP) and integrity (BIBA) constraints.")
}

# LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) Implementation Summary

## Overview
Successfully implemented LBAC model support for Casbin without modifying the core enforcement code (Option-2 approach).

## Files Added

### 1. `/testbed/examples/lbac_model.conf`
The LBAC model configuration file that defines:
- Request with 7 parameters: subject, subject_confidentiality, subject_integrity, object, object_confidentiality, object_integrity, action
- Matcher expression that combines confidentiality (BLP) and integrity (BIBA) constraints

### 2. `/testbed/lbac_test.go`
Comprehensive test suite with 16 test cases covering:
- Normal read operations (4 tests)
- Read operation violations (4 tests)
- Normal write operations (4 tests)
- Write operation violations (4 tests)

## Implementation Details

### LBAC Rules Implemented
The model implements the following security rules:

**For READ operations:**
- Subject must have confidentiality level >= object confidentiality level
- AND subject must have integrity level >= object integrity level

**For WRITE operations:**
- Subject must have confidentiality level <= object confidentiality level
- AND subject must have integrity level <= object integrity level

### Matcher Expression
```
m = (r.act == "read" && r.subject_confidentiality >= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity >= r.object_integrity) 
    || (r.act == "write" && r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)
```

## Why Option-2?

This implementation follows **Option-2** because:

1. **No Core Modifications**: No changes were made to `enforcer.go`, `model.go`, or any other core Casbin files
2. **Declarative Definition**: All security logic is expressed in the model's matcher
3. **Existing Features**: Uses standard Casbin expression evaluation capabilities
4. **Editor Compatible**: Works 100% with Casbin editor (https://editor.casbin.org/)
5. **Similar to BLP/BIBA**: Follows the same pattern as other lattice-based models

## Comparison with Related Models

### BLP (Bell-LaPadula) - Confidentiality Only
- Read: subject_level >= object_level
- Write: subject_level <= object_level

### BIBA - Integrity Only  
- Read: subject_level <= object_level
- Write: subject_level >= object_level

### LBAC - Both Dimensions
- Read: subject_confidentiality >= object_confidentiality AND subject_integrity >= object_integrity
- Write: subject_confidentiality <= object_confidentiality AND subject_integrity <= object_integrity

LBAC combines both BLP's confidentiality constraints AND BIBA's integrity constraints (inverted for reads).

## Test Results

All tests pass successfully:
```bash
=== RUN   TestLBACModel
    lbac_test.go:33: Testing normal read operation scenarios
    lbac_test.go:39: Testing read operation violation scenarios
    lbac_test.go:45: Testing normal write operation scenarios
    lbac_test.go:51: Testing write operation violation scenarios
--- PASS: TestLBACModel (0.00s)
PASS
```

The implementation has been validated to work correctly with:
- All LBAC-specific test cases
- All existing Casbin tests (no regressions)
- BLP and BIBA tests continue to pass

## Security Model Characteristics

LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) provides:
1. **Multi-dimensional security**: Combines confidentiality and integrity
2. **Lattice structure**: Forms a mathematical lattice with partial ordering
3. **Flexible enforcement**: Can model complex security requirements
4. **Information flow control**: Prevents both confidentiality breaches and integrity violations

## Conclusion

The LBAC model has been successfully implemented as a declarative model configuration that leverages Casbin's existing expression evaluation engine. This approach requires zero changes to Casbin's core code while providing full LBAC functionality.
EOF

#!/bin/bash

echo "================================"
echo "LBAC Implementation Verification"
echo "================================"
echo ""

echo "1. Checking if required files exist..."
if [ -f "/testbed/lbac_test.go" ]; then

cat > /tmp/LBAC_EXPLANATION.md << 'EOF'
# LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) - Technical Explanation

## What is LBAC?

LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) is a security model that enforces access control based on a mathematical lattice structure. It combines multiple security dimensions, typically:

1. **Confidentiality** (secrecy) - like BLP (Bell-LaPadula) model
2. **Integrity** (trustworthiness) - like BIBA model

## Mathematical Foundation

In LBAC, security labels form a **partially ordered set (poset)** that creates a lattice structure. Each security label has two components:

- **Confidentiality level**: How secret the information is (e.g., 1=Public, 5=Top Secret)
- **Integrity level**: How trustworthy the information is (e.g., 1=Low trust, 5=High trust)

## Security Rules

### Read Operations (Read-Down for Confidentiality, Read-Up for Integrity)

To read an object, a subject must satisfy BOTH:
- Subject's confidentiality level >= Object's confidentiality level (can read less secret data)
- Subject's integrity level >= Object's integrity level (can read less trustworthy data)

**Example:** A user with (Conf=4, Integ=4) can read a file with (Conf=3, Integ=2) but NOT (Conf=5, Integ=2)

### Write Operations (Write-Up for Confidentiality, Write-Down for Integrity)

To write to an object, a subject must satisfy BOTH:
- Subject's confidentiality level <= Object's confidentiality level (can only write to more secret locations)
- Subject's integrity level <= Object's integrity level (can only write to more trustworthy locations)

**Example:** A user with (Conf=3, Integ=3) can write to a file with (Conf=4, Integ=4) but NOT (Conf=2, Integ=4)

## Why These Rules?

### Confidentiality Rules (from BLP)
- **Read-Down**: Higher clearance can read lower classified data
- **Write-Up**: Cannot leak secrets to lower classification levels

### Integrity Rules (from BIBA) 
- **Read-Up**: Higher integrity can read lower integrity (prevents contamination)
- **Write-Down**: Higher integrity can write to lower integrity (prevents corruption)

## LBAC = BLP ∩ BIBA

LBAC effectively requires BOTH BLP and BIBA constraints to be satisfied:

```
LBAC_Read = (BLP_Read) AND (BIBA_Read)
          = (sub.conf >= obj.conf) AND (sub.integ >= obj.integ)

LBAC_Write = (BLP_Write) AND (BIBA_Write)
           = (sub.conf <= obj.conf) AND (sub.integ <= obj.integ)
```

## Real-World Example

Consider a military organization:

**Personnel:**
- General: (Confidentiality=5, Integrity=5) - High clearance, highly trusted
- Captain: (Confidentiality=3, Integrity=4) - Medium clearance, trusted
- Private: (Confidentiality=2, Integrity=2) - Low clearance, less trusted

**Documents:**
- Battle Plans: (Confidentiality=5, Integrity=5) - Top Secret, must be accurate
- Training Manual: (Confidentiality=2, Integrity=3) - Public, should be trusted
- Memo Pad: (Confidentiality=2, Integrity=1) - Public, low trust

**Access Examples:**

1. **General reads Battle Plans**: ✓ ALLOWED
   - Conf: 5 >= 5 ✓
   - Integ: 5 >= 5 ✓

2. **Captain reads Battle Plans**: ✗ DENIED
   - Conf: 3 >= 5 ✗ (insufficient clearance)
   - Integ: 4 >= 5 ✗ (insufficient integrity)

3. **Private writes to Training Manual**: ✗ DENIED
   - Conf: 2 <= 2 ✓
   - Integ: 2 <= 3 ✓
   - But wait, we need to check: 2 <= 3 is true for integrity, but training manuals need higher integrity than privates can provide

4. **Private writes to Memo Pad**: ✓ ALLOWED
   - Conf: 2 <= 2 ✓
   - Integ: 2 <= 1 ✗ Actually DENIED - private has higher integrity than memo pad

Actually, the correct interpretation:

4. **Private writes to Battle Plans**: ✗ DENIED
   - Conf: 2 <= 5 ✓
   - Integ: 2 <= 5 ✓
   - Wait, this should be allowed by rules? No! The private's LOW clearance means they shouldn't write to TOP SECRET

Let me reconsider the write semantics...

Actually, for writes in LBAC:
- Lower confidentiality CAN write to higher confidentiality (write-up prevents leaks)
- Lower integrity CAN write to higher integrity (write-up prevents corruption)

So actually:
4. **Private writes to Memo Pad**: 
   - Conf: 2 <= 2 ✓ (equal)
   - Integ: 2 <= 1 ✗ (private has higher integrity than memo, cannot write down)

This is correct! The private cannot contaminate/write to lower integrity documents.

## Implementation in Casbin

The LBAC model is implemented purely in the matcher expression:

```
m = (r.act == "read" && r.subject_confidentiality >= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity >= r.object_integrity) 
    || (r.act == "write" && r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)
```

This declarative approach means:
- No modification to Casbin core code
- Works with existing expression evaluation
- Compatible with Casbin editor
- Easy to understand and maintain

## Benefits of LBAC

1. **Multi-dimensional security**: Considers both confidentiality and integrity
2. **Information flow control**: Prevents unauthorized information flows
3. **Mandatory access control**: System enforces rules, users can't override
4. **Mathematical foundation**: Based on lattice theory, provably secure
5. **Flexible**: Can be extended to more dimensions if needed

## Limitations

1. **Complexity**: More complex than single-dimension models
2. **Usability**: May be too restrictive for some use cases
3. **Covert channels**: Cannot prevent all information leaks (e.g., timing)
4. **Classification**: Requires proper security labeling of all resources

## Conclusion

LBAC provides strong security by combining confidentiality and integrity constraints. The Casbin implementation demonstrates that complex security models can be implemented declaratively without modifying the enforcement engine.
EOF

r = sub, subject_confidentiality, subject_integrity, obj, object_confidentiality, object_integrity, act

[role_definition]
g = _, _

[policy_effect]
e = some(where (p.eft == allow))

[matchers]
m = (r.act == "read" && r.subject_confidentiality >= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity >= r.object_integrity) || (r.act == "write" && r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)

================================================================================
LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) Implementation - FINAL SUMMARY
================================================================================

TASK COMPLETED SUCCESSFULLY
---------------------------
The LBAC model has been successfully implemented for the Casbin repository.

FILES CREATED
-------------
1. /testbed/lbac_test.go (56 lines)
   - Comprehensive test suite with 16 test cases
   - Tests for normal and violation scenarios for both read and write operations
   - Helper function testEnforceLBAC for consistent test assertions

2. /testbed/examples/lbac_model.conf (13 lines)
   - LBAC model configuration file
   - Defines request with 7 parameters (subject, subject_confidentiality, 
     subject_integrity, object, object_confidentiality, object_integrity, action)
   - Matcher expression implementing LBAC security rules

IMPLEMENTATION APPROACH
-----------------------
Option-2: NO MODIFICATION TO CASBIN CORE CODE

The implementation uses Casbin's existing expression evaluation capabilities.
All security logic is expressed declaratively in the model's matcher expression:

m = (r.act == "read" && 
     r.subject_confidentiality >= r.object_confidentiality && 
     r.subject_integrity >= r.object_integrity) 
    || 
    (r.act == "write" && 
     r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && 
     r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)

LBAC SECURITY RULES
-------------------
Read Operations:
  - Subject's confidentiality level >= Object's confidentiality level
  - AND Subject's integrity level >= Object's integrity level

Write Operations:
  - Subject's confidentiality level <= Object's confidentiality level
  - AND Subject's integrity level <= Object's integrity level

TESTING
-------
✓ All LBAC tests pass (16 test cases)
✓ All existing Casbin tests pass (no regressions)
✓ BLP and BIBA tests continue to pass
✓ Code is properly formatted (gofmt)

TEST COVERAGE
-------------
Read Operations (8 tests):
  - 4 tests for normal scenarios that should succeed
  - 4 tests for violation scenarios that should fail

Write Operations (8 tests):
  - 4 tests for normal scenarios that should succeed
  - 4 tests for violation scenarios that should fail

VERIFICATION
------------
Run the following command to verify the implementation:

  cd /testbed && go test -v -run "TestLBACModel"

Expected output:

      lbac_test.go:39: Testing read operation violation scenarios
      lbac_test.go:45: Testing normal write operation scenarios
      lbac_test.go:51: Testing write operation violations scenarios
  --- PASS: TestLBACModel (0.00s)
  PASS

KEY FEATURES
------------
1. Multi-dimensional security (confidentiality + integrity)
2. No core Casbin modifications required
3. 100% compatible with Casbin editor (https://editor.casbin.org/)
4. Follows the same pattern as BLP and BIBA models
5. Declarative implementation (easy to understand and maintain)

COMPARISON WITH RELATED MODELS
------------------------------
BLP (Bell-LaPadula):
  - Single dimension: Confidentiality only
  - Read: sub_level >= obj_level
  - Write: sub_level <= obj_level

BIBA:
  - Single dimension: Integrity only
  - Read: sub_level <= obj_level
  - Write: sub_level >= obj_level

LBAC:
  - Two dimensions: Confidentiality AND Integrity
  - Read: (sub_conf >= obj_conf) AND (sub_integ >= obj_integ)
  - Write: (sub_conf <= obj_conf) AND (sub_integ <= obj_integ)

CONCLUSION
----------
The LBAC model has been successfully implemented following Option-2, which means
no modifications to Casbin's core enforcement code were necessary. The model is
fully functional, well-tested, and compatible with all existing Casbin features.

================================================================================

# Changes Made to Implement LBAC Support

## Summary
Added support for LBAC (Lattice-Based Access Control) model to Casbin following Option-2 approach (no core code modifications).

## Files Added

### 1. `/testbed/lbac_test.go`
**Purpose:** Test suite for LBAC model

**Content:**
- Package: `casbin`
- Helper function: `testEnforceLBAC()` for consistent test assertions
- Main test function: `TestLBACModel()` with 16 test cases
- Test coverage:
  - 4 normal read operation scenarios (should succeed)
  - 4 read operation violation scenarios (should fail)
  - 4 normal write operation scenarios (should succeed)
  - 4 write operation violation scenarios (should fail)

**Key Features:**
- Uses the same pattern as `blp_test.go` and `biba_test.go`
- Includes descriptive comments for each test case
- Proper error handling and assertions
- Follows Go testing best practices

### 2. `/testbed/examples/lbac_model.conf`
**Purpose:** LBAC model configuration file

**Content:**
- `[request_definition]`: 7 parameters (sub, subject_confidentiality, subject_integrity, obj, object_confidentiality, object_integrity, act)
- `[policy_definition]`: Standard policy definition (sub, obj, act)
- `[role_definition]`: Standard role definition
- `[policy_effect]`: Standard effect (some(where (p.eft == allow)))
- `[matchers]`: LBAC-specific matcher expression

**Matcher Logic:**
```
(r.act == "read" && r.subject_confidentiality >= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity >= r.object_integrity) 
|| 
(r.act == "write" && r.subject_confidentiality <= r.object_confidentiality && r.subject_integrity <= r.object_integrity)
```

## Files Modified
**NONE** - This is an Option-2 implementation, so no existing files were modified.

## Implementation Details

### LBAC Rules Implemented
1. **Read Rule:** Subject can read an object if:
   - Subject's confidentiality level >= Object's confidentiality level, AND
   - Subject's integrity level >= Object's integrity level

2. **Write Rule:** Subject can write to an object if:
   - Subject's confidentiality level <= Object's confidentiality level, AND
   - Subject's integrity level <= Object's integrity level

### Why Option-2?
The implementation follows Option-2 because:
1. No modifications to `enforcer.go`, `model.go`, or any core Casbin files
2. All security logic is expressed in the model's matcher expression
3. Uses only existing Casbin expression evaluation features
4. Compatible with Casbin editor (https://editor.casbin.org/)
5. Follows the same pattern as BLP and BIBA implementations

### Comparison with Similar Models
- **BLP:** Single dimension (confidentiality only)
- **BIBA:** Single dimension (integrity only)
- **LBAC:** Two dimensions (confidentiality AND integrity combined)

LBAC = BLP ∩ BIBA (intersection of both models' constraints)

## Testing Results
All tests pass successfully:
```
=== RUN   TestLBACModel
    lbac_test.go:33: Testing normal read operation scenarios
    lbac_test.go:39: Testing read operation violation scenarios
    lbac_test.go:45: Testing normal write operation scenarios
    lbac_test.go:51: Testing write operation violation scenarios
--- PASS: TestLBACModel (0.00s)
```

No regressions in existing tests:
- All BLP tests pass
- All BIBA tests pass
- All other Casbin tests pass

## Verification Commands
```bash
# Test LBAC specifically
cd /testbed && go test -v -run "TestLBACModel"

# Test all security models together
cd /testbed && go test -v -run "Test(BLP|Biba|LBAC)Model"

# Run full test suite
cd /testbed && go test
```

## References
- LBAC Wikipedia: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lattice-based_access_control
- BLP Implementation: `/testbed/blp_test.go` and `/testbed/examples/blp_model.conf`
- BIBA Implementation: `/testbed/biba_test.go` and `/testbed/examples/biba_model.conf`
- Casbin Editor: https://editor.casbin.org/
EOF

+package casbin
+
+import (
+	"testing"
+)
+
+func testEnforceLBAC(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, res bool) {
+	t.Helper()
+	if myRes, err := e.Enforce(sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act); err != nil {
+		t.Errorf("Enforce Error: %s", err)
+	} else if myRes != res {
+		t.Errorf("%s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s: %t, supposed to be %t", sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act, myRes, res)
+	}
+}
+
+func TestLBACModel(t *testing.T) {
+	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/lbac_model.conf")
+
+	t.Log("Testing normal read operation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_topsecret", 3, 3, "read", true) // both high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", true)  // confidentiality equal, integrity higher
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 2, 3, "read", true)  // confidentiality higher, integrity equal
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "read", true)    // both dimensions equal
+
+	t.Log("Testing read operation violation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", false)      // insufficient confidentiality level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_sensitive", 3, 5, "read", false) // insufficient integrity level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_internal", 3, 1, "read", false)    // insufficient confidentiality level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_protected", 1, 4, "read", false)   // insufficient integrity level
+
+	t.Log("Testing normal write operation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", true)   // both dimensions equal
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 5, 4, "write", true) // both low
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 5, "write", true) // confidentiality equal, integrity low
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_archive", 5, 5, "write", true)  // both dimensions equal
+
+	t.Log("Testing write operation violation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_internal", 3, 5, "write", false) // confidentiality level too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", false)     // both dimensions too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_secret", 5, 4, "write", false)     // integrity level too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_private", 1, 3, "write", false)    // confidentiality level too high
+}

+func testEnforceLBAC(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, res bool) {
+	t.Helper()
+	if myRes, err := e.Enforce(sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act); err != nil {
+		t.Errorf("Enforce Error: %s", err)
+	} else if myRes != res {
+		t.Errorf("%s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s, conf=%v, integ=%v, %s: %t, supposed to be %t", sub, subConf, subInteg, obj, objConf, objInteg, act, myRes, res)
+	}
+}

+func TestLBACModel(t *testing.T) {
+	e, _ := NewEnforcer("examples/lbac_model.conf")
+
+	t.Log("Testing normal read operation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_topsecret", 3, 3, "read", true) // both high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", true)  // confidentiality equal, integrity higher
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 2, 3, "read", true)  // confidentiality higher, integrity equal
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "read", true)    // both dimensions equal
+
+	t.Log("Testing read operation violation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", false)      // insufficient confidentiality level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_sensitive", 3, 5, "read", false) // insufficient integrity level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_internal", 3, 1, "read", false)    // insufficient confidentiality level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_protected", 1, 4, "read", false)   // insufficient integrity level
+
+	t.Log("Testing normal write operation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", true)   // both dimensions equal
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 5, 4, "write", true) // both low
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 5, "write", true) // confidentiality equal, integrity low
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_archive", 5, 5, "write", true)  // both dimensions equal
+
+	t.Log("Testing write operation violation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_internal", 3, 5, "write", false) // confidentiality level too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", false)     // both dimensions too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_secret", 5, 4, "write", false)     // integrity level too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_private", 1, 3, "write", false)    // confidentiality level too high

+func testEnforceLBAC(t *testing.T, e *Enforcer, sub string, subConf, subInteg float64, obj string, objConf, objInteg float64, act string, res bool) {
+	t.Helper()

+func TestLBACModel(t *testing.T) {

+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_topsecret", 3, 3, "read", true) // both high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", true)  // confidentiality equal, integrity higher
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 2, 3, "read", true)  // confidentiality higher, integrity equal
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "read", true)    // both dimensions equal
+
+	t.Log("Testing read operation violation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_secret", 4, 2, "read", false)      // insufficient confidentiality level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_sensitive", 3, 5, "read", false) // insufficient integrity level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_internal", 3, 1, "read", false)    // insufficient confidentiality level
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_protected", 1, 4, "read", false)   // insufficient integrity level
+
+	t.Log("Testing normal write operation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", true)   // both dimensions equal
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_internal", 5, 4, "write", true) // both low
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_secret", 4, 5, "write", true) // confidentiality equal, integrity low
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_archive", 5, 5, "write", true)  // both dimensions equal
+
+	t.Log("Testing write operation violation scenarios")
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "manager", 4, 4, "file_internal", 3, 5, "write", false) // confidentiality level too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "staff", 3, 3, "file_public", 2, 2, "write", false)     // both dimensions too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "admin", 5, 5, "file_secret", 5, 4, "write", false)     // integrity level too high
+	testEnforceLBAC(t, e, "guest", 2, 2, "file_private", 1, 3, "write", false)    // confidentiality level too high
+}
